117195 6Selects the GPIB bus on which to perform the operation.  The VI addresses the interface indicated by bus as a Listener.  If you have only one GPIB interface in your computer, the default bus number is 0. For additional GPIB interfaces, see the software installation instructions included with your GPIB board.
117510 Termination mode specifies how the GPIB driver should determine when the read is finished.  All values from 0-255 (0x0-0xFF) will be taken to be an eos byte which wll stop the read when it is recieved in the data stream or when end is detected.  STOPend 256 (0x100) (the default) indicates to stop the read when end is detected.  The read  will always stop when the requested count has been read.
117910 status is a Boolean array in which each bit describes a state of the GPIB Controller. If an error occurs, the GPIB VIs set bit 15. GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set.
118094 GPIB status vector:
118115 status[0] - Device Clear State
118146  status[1] - Device Trigger State
118180  status[2] - Listener Active State
118216 status[3] - Talker Active State
118249 status[4] - Attention line asserted
118286 status[5] -
118298 Controller In Charge
118319  status[6] - Remote State
118345  status[7] - Lockout State
118373 status[8] - I/O Completed 
118401 status[9] - not used
118422  status[10]- not used
118444  status[11]- not used
118467 status[12]- SRQ line asserted when CIC
118507 status[13]- EOI or EOS detected
118539  status[14]- Timeout occured
118568  status[15]- GPIB error detected
118604 GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set.
118657 GPIB Error:
118674 -No error
118689 -Function requires GPIB to be CIC
118728 -No listeners detected on write
118765 -Controller not addressed correctly
118806 -Invalid argument(s)
118833 (perhaps bad address string????)
118871 -Function requires GPIB to be SC
118909 -I/O operation aborted
118937 -hardware not present
118964 -DMA error
118980 -DMA bus timeout
119002 -New I/O attempted while I/O in 
119041 progress
119055 -function not implemented
119086 -file system error
119110 -shareable board exclusively owned
119150 -GPIB bus error (commands)
119182 -Serial Poll Byte Lost
119210 -SRQ line cannot be cleared
119243 -Unrecognized commandEAbyte count refers to the number of bytes that pass over the GPIB.
119333 This integer represents a GPIB address.  The low byte is the primary GPIB address (0-30) and the high byte is either 0 or a secondary GPIB address (96-126 or 0x60-0x7E).  Use MakeAddress.vi to construct a GPIB address which uses secondary addressing.RNcount. The VI returns up to count data bytes from the device in data string. 
119667 GPIB status vector:
119688 status[0] - Device Clear State
119719  status[1] - Device Trigger State
119753  status[2] - Listener Active State
119789 status[3] - Talker Active State
119822 status[4] - Attention line asserted
119859 status[5] -
119871 Controller In Charge
119892  status[6] - Remote State
119918  status[7] - Lockout State
119946 status[8] - I/O Completed 
119974 status[9] - not used
119995  status[10]- not used
120017  status[11]- not used
120040 status[12]- SRQ line asserted when CIC
120080 status[13]- EOI or EOS detected
120112  status[14]- Timeout occured
120141  status[15]- GPIB error detectedA=data string contains count data bytes from the GPIB device.

177096 -Serial Poll Byte Lost
177124 -SRQ line cannot be cleared
177157 -Unrecognized commandEAbyte count refers to the number of bytes that pass over the GPIB.
177249 status is a Boolean array in which each bit describes a state of the GPIB Controller. If an error occurs, the GPIB VIs set bit 15. GPIB error is valid only if bit 15 of status is set.
177433 GPIB status vector:
177454 status[0] - Device Clear State
177485  status[1] - Device Trigger State
177519  status[2] - Listener Active State
177555 status[3] - Talker Active State
177588 status[4] - Attention line asserted
177625 status[5] -
177637 Controller In Charge
177658  status[6] - Remote State
177684  status[7] - Lockout State
177712 status[8] - I/O Completed 
177740 status[9] - not used
177761  status[10]- not used
177783  status[11]- not used
177806 status[12]- SRQ line asserted when CIC
177846 status[13]- EOI or EOS detected
177878  status[14]- Timeout occured
177907  status[15]- GPIB error detected
177941 This integer represents a GPIB address.  The low byte is the primary GPIB address (0-30) and the high byte is either 0 or a secondary GPIB address (96-126 or 0x60-0x7E).  Use MakeAddress.vi to construct a GPIB address which uses secondary addressing.
178194 3Selects the GPIB bus on which to perform the operation.  The VI addresses the interface indicated by bus as a Talker. If you have only one GPIB interface in your computer, the default bus number is 0. For additional GPIB interfaces, see the software installation instructions included with your GPIB board.
178504 The end of transfer mode describes the method of signaling the end of the data to the listener.  Its values are:
178617   2 (default) DABend - Send eoi with last byte.
178665  1 NL end - Send linefeed with eoi after data.
178712  0 NULLend - Do nothing at end of transfer.OKdata string contains the data bytes that the VI sends to the GPIB device.

284686 | *`
284694 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
285039      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
285091      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
285149      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
285206      error, and a positive value is a warning.
285254      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
285304      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
285353 1-(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred."
285403 no error

285418 no error
285427 ERROR
285436 (i32) The error code associated with an error.  Possible values:
285502 0  Success
285513 -1200  Invalid syntax string
285542 -1201  Error finding instruments
285575 -1202  Unable to initialize interface or instrument
285627 -1205  Invalid instr handle
285655 -1210  Parameter out of range
285685 -1220  Error getting attribute
285716 -1221  Error setting attribute
285747 -1224  Error clearing instrument
285780 -1225  Error triggering instrument
285815 -1226  Error polling instrument
285847 -1230  Error writing to instrument
285882 -1231  Error reading from instrument
285919 -1240  Instrument timed out
285947 -1250  Error mapping VXI address
285980 -1251  Error unmapping VXI address
286015 -1252  Error accessing VXIbus
286045 -1260  Function not supported by controller
286089 [W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.

431498 /Primary GPIB address ranging from 0 to 30.  Used to form the low order byte of the GPIB address which will be accepted by 488.2 functions.  The value of 31 (default) means return the NOADDR constant (0xFFFF) as the packed address.  The VI places primary address in the lower byte of the packed address.
431806 Secondary GPIB address ranging from 0 to 30.  Used to form the high order byte of the GPIB address which will be accepted by 488.2 functions. The value of 31 (default) means use no secondary address. The VI places secondary address in the upper byte of the packed address.
432082 VThis integer represents a GPIB address.  The low byte is the primary GPIB address (0-30) and the high byte is either 0 or a secondary GPIB address (96-126 or 0x60-0x7E).  packed address contains primary address in its lower byte and secondary address in its upper byte. You can use packed address as the address input to the GPIB 488.2 VIs. 
432427 True if either primary or secondary addresses are outside ot the range 0-31.  address error indicates whether a range error has occurred.

443660 Initializes the software connection to the instrument.  In the case of VXI instruments controlled via NI-VXI, initializes the NI-VXI library, reads in the resource manager table, calculates A16 configuration addresses, determines memory requirements, and stores base addresses into A24 or A32 space.  For VXI instruments controlled via GPIB-VXI, performs all of the above except initialization of NI-VXI libraries.  You must run the INSTR Close VI once for every time you run this VI.

476853 A unique reference to an instrument I/O session.  It identifies which device to communicate with and all configuration information to perform the I/O.  An instr handle is returned from the Instr Open VI or the Initialize VI of an instrument driver.
477105 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
477450      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
477502      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
477560      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
477617      error, and a positive value is a warning.
477665      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
477715      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
477764 [W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.1-(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred."

587761 instr vtl global
588066 Initializes the software connection to the instrument.  In the case of VXI instruments controlled via NI-VXI, initializes the NI-VXI library, reads in the resource manager table, calculates A16 configuration addresses, determines memory requirements, and stores base addresses into A24 or A32 space.  For VXI instruments controlled via GPIB-VXI, performs all of the above except initialization of NI-VXI libraries.  You must run the INSTR Close VI once for every time you run this VI.$

628000 (I32) 
628007 A unique reference to an instrument I/O session.  It identifies which device to communicate with and all configuration information to perform the I/O.  An instr handle is returned from the Instr Open VI or the Initialize VI of an instrument driver.
628259 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
628604      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
628656      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
628714      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
628771      error, and a positive value is a warning.
628819      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
628869      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
628918 [W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.1-(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred."

629278 f(cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  If an error has already occurred, this VI does nothing.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
629536      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.

737715 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
738060      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
738112      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
738170      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
738227      error, and a positive value is a warning.
738275      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
738325      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
738374 [W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.1-(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
738514 (ABC) Uniquely identifies the instrument to establish communications with.  The grammar for the instrument descriptor is shown below.  Parameters are shown in lower-case and optional parameters are shown in square brackets ([]).
738744 GPIB:   INSTR{GPIB[bd]::prim addr[::sec addr]}
738791 VXI:  INSTR{VXI::logical addr}
738822 GPIB-VXI:   INSTR{GPIB-VXI[bd]::logical addr[prim addr]}
738880 Optional Parameter Default Values:
738915     bd - GPIB board (0)
738939     prim addr - GPIB primary address (1)
738980     sec addr - GPIB secondary address (none)
739025     logical addr - VXI logical address 
739066 EXAMPLE:  A GPIB instrument on GPIB board 0, at primary address 5, and no secondary addressing.
739164 INSTR{GPIB::5}"

739212 (ABC) 
739219 The name of the VI that is calling this VI.  If an error occurs during the operation of this VI, the value in source will be placed in the source element of the error out cluster. 
739402 (I32) 
739409 A unique reference to an instrument I/O session.  It identifies which device to communicate with and all configuration information to perform the I/O.  An instr handle is returned from the Instr Open VI or the Initialize VI of an instrument driver.
739660 f(cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  If an error has already occurred, this VI does nothing.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
739918      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
739969      If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing.
740016      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
740074      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
740131      error, and a positive value is a warning.
740179      (ABC) source:  an indication of where an 
740226      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
740275 ZV(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred. If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing."

804276 VISA session (for class)
804309 This VI loads the addressing information about the instrument into the Open VXI Instrument VI and returns the instrument ID.  You can reset the instrument by setting the front panel reset control.  You must run this VI before using any of the instrument driver VIs for this instrument.
804597 (I32) 
804604 A unique reference to an instrument I/O session.  It identifies which device to communicate with and all configuration information to perform the I/O.  An instr handle is returned from the Instr Open VI or the Initialize VI of an instrument driver.
804855 f(cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  If an error has already occurred, this VI does nothing.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
805113      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
805164      If status is TRUE, this VI does nothing.
805211      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
805269      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
805326      error, and a positive value is a warning.
805374      (ABC) source:  an indication of where an 
805421      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
805472 The status boolean is either TRUE (X) for an error, or FALSE (checkmark) for no error or a warning.
805573 The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.
805677 The code input identifies the error or warning.
805726 The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.
805830 The source string describes the origin of the error or warning.
805895 The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.
806001 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
806346      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
806398      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
806456      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an
806513      error, and a positive value is a warning.
806561      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
806611      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
806662 The status boolean is either TRUE (X) for an error, or FALSE (checkmark) for no error or a warning.
806763 The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.
806867 The source string describes the origin of the error or warning.
806932 The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.
807036 The code input identifies the error or warning.
807085 The pop-up option Explain Error (or Explain Warning) gives more information about the error displayed.

837847 5Generalized DIO96 control.
837876 Device:  Card ID.
837894 Port Number: (0-11); APA=0, APB=1,APC=2,BPA=3,...
837944 Port Width: Width of port in # of bits.
837984 Initialize: If zero, port will be initialized.
838031 Input: Data, if any, to be written to the port.
838079 Read/Write: Bool., F=Read, T=Write.
838115 Output: Data written to or read from port.
838168 Most applications need only connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.  Connections to other controls and indicators are useful only if specifically needed.
838347 The Read from Digital Port VI reads a user configured digital port.  The reading is displayed as a binary number in [pattern].
838475 You have the option to not reconfigure the port as an input port by setting the iteration control to a non-zero value. You can also concatenate multiple ports to operate as one large port by using the port width paramter.
838698 Port Width for the Lab boards, SCXI-1200, DAQBox-1200, DIO-24, DIO-32F, DIO-96, and AT-MIO-16D ports 2, 3 and 4 should be at least 8.
838833 Please read the DAQ VI Reference Manual for descriptions of Digital Port Configure and Digital Port Read for more information.
838968 Most applications need only connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.  Connections to other controls and indicators are useful only if specifically needed.
839147 The Write to Digital Port VI outputs a pattern (in binary) to a specified digital port.  
839238 You can control the number of lines in a port by the parameter port width.  You also have the option of not reconfiguring the port as an output port with each iteration of the VI by setting the iteration control to a non-zero value.
839472 Port Width for the Lab boards, SCXI-1200, DAQBox-1200, DIO-24, DIO-32F, DIO-96, and AT-MIO-16D ports 2, 3 and 4 should be at least 8. 
839608 Please read the DAQ VI Reference Manual for descriptions of Digital Port Configure and Digital Port Write for more information.
839743 1This error handler is used primarily to inform the user if an input error exists, to describe the error, and to identify where it occurred.  The information for this is derived from the inputs error in, error code, and error source, and from an internal error description table.  The table describes all errors that can be created by LabVIEW or its associated I/O operations.  The handler has provisions to take alternative actions, such as to cancel or set an error status, and to test for and describe user-defined errors.  See instruction on the front panel.
840316 For most applications, you only need to connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.

840707 ZFor most applications, you only need to connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.

901969 VFor most applications, you only need to connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.
902075 This VI writes the value in pattern to the port identified by task ID.
902147 See the Data Acquisition VI Reference Manual for your platform for tables listing the default settings and ranges for this VI for the boards with which it will work.84(u32) task ID: identifies the group and I/O pattern.D@(u32) pattern: specifies the new state of the lines in the port.
902435 x(i32) line mask: determines which lines in the port the write affects. If you set line mask to -1, the VI writes to the entire port and sets all the lines in the port to the states specified by the bits in pattern. If you set only bit n in line mask, the VI changes only line n in the port to the state that bit n of pattern specifies. The default setting for line mask is -1.51(u32) task ID out: has the same value as task ID.

932030 This VI reads the port identified by task ID and returns the pattern read.
932106 See the Data Acquisition VI Reference Manual for your platform for tables listing the default settings and ranges for this VI for the boards with which it will work.
932275 (i32) line mask: determines which lines this VI reads. If you set line mask to -1 (all ones), the VI reads the entire port. If you set only bit n in line mask, the VI reads only line n of the port. If the state of line n is high, the VI sets bit n of pattern. The VI sets to 0 the bits of pattern that correspond to lines the VI has not read. The default setting for line mask is -1 which is shown as all ones since the binary representation is the default selection.62(u32) pattern: the data the VI read from the port.51(u32) task ID out: has the same value as task ID.
932849 (cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
933049      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
933101      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
933159      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an 
933217      error, and a positive value is a warning.
933265      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
933315      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
933364 xt(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred. Regardless of the value of status, this VI clears the input operation.
933484 (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.  A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an error, and a positive value is a warning.[W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
933724 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
934069      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.

934237      error, and a positive value is a warning.

963204 This VI establishes a port configuration. You can use the task ID that this VI returns only in digital port VIs.
963318 See the Data Acquisition VI Reference Manual for your platform for tables listing the default settings and ranges for this VI for the boards with which it will work.gc(i16) device: the device number you assigned to the data acquisition device when you configured it.
963587 /(i16) port width: the total width in bits of the port. For example, you can combine two 4-bit ports into an 8-bit port on an MIO board by setting port width to 8.
963752 When port width is greater than the physical port width of a digital port, the following restrictions apply. The port width must be an integral multiple of the physical port width, and the port numbers in the combined port must begin with the port named by port number and must increase consecutively. For example, if port  number is 3 and port width is 24 (bits), the VI uses ports 3, 4, and 5.
964150 ?(i32) line direction map: specifies the direction of each line in the port. If a bit is 0 in the line map, the line is an input line. If a bit is 1, the line is an output line. Setting line direction map to -1 makes all the lines in a port output lines. Setting line direction map to 0 makes all the lines in a port input lines. Except for the NB-TIO-10 and PC-TIO-10, this is how you must use line direction map. The NB-TIO-10 and PC-TIO-10 are the only boards on which you can configure lines within a port for different directions. The default for line direction map is 0.
964728 (u32) task ID: uniquely identifies the group. You use this value as the task ID to refer to this group in subsequent digital port VI calls.
964871 (cluster) error in:  a cluster describing any error conditions prior to this VI's execution.  The default input of this cluster is no error.  The error in cluster contains the following parameters: 
965071      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
965123      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
965181      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an 
965239      error, and a positive value is a warning.
965287      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
965337      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
965386 xt(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred. Regardless of the value of status, this VI clears the input operation.
965507 D(string) port number: specifies the port this VI configures. A port number value of 0 signifies port 0, a port number of 1 signifies port 1, and so on. If you use an SCXI-1160, SCXI-1161, SCXI-1162, or SCXI-1163 module, use the SCx!MDy syntax, where x is the chassis and y is the module device number, to specify the module.
965834 (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.  A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an error, and a positive value is a warning.[W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
966074 (cluster) error out:  a cluster containing error information.  If error in indicated an error, error out contains the same error information.  Otherwise, it describes the error status of this VI.  Use the General Error Handler utility VI to check the error at the end of your diagram.  The error out cluster contains the following parameters: 
966419      (bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
966471      (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.
966529      A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an 
966587      error, and a positive value is a warning.
966635      (string) source:  an indication of where an 
966685      error occurred, usually the name of the VI.
966734 1-(bool) status: TRUE if an error has occurred.
966783 (i32) code: the error code associated with an error.  A value of 0 means no error, a negative value is an error, and a positive value is a warning.[W(string) source:  an indication of where an error occurred, usually the name of the VI.

1028048 QDSP NumBytesGTZero:  The number of bytes to allocate should be greater than zero.SDSP InvalidDataType:  The data type can only be 4 bytes long(0) or 2 bytes long(1).
1028215 DSP IndexSizeOffsetErr:  The size+offset should be less than or equal to the size of the DSP Handle Structure which you index into.[DSP IndexSizeGTZero:  The size of the New DSP Handle Structure should be greater than zero.FDSP OffsetGEZero:  The offset should be greater than or equal to zero.KDSP CopyNumGTZero:  The number of data to copy should be greater than zero.uDSP Invalid CopyType:  The entire/partial copy selector can only select between entire copy (0) and partial copy (1).GDSP PathnameTooLong:  The path name should be less than 256 characters.
1028776 DSP InvalidArrayType:  The array type can only be 32-bit floating point data(0), 16-bit long integer data(1) or 32-bit short integer data(2).:DSP AllocArrayFailed:  Failed to allocate a LabVIEW array.2DSP SourceNumErr:  You can only select one source.bDSP InvalidBytesSelect:  bytes/element selector can only select between 4 bytes(0) and 2 bytes(1).nDSP ErrInGetFunctionHandle:  An error occurred when calling the function GetIndirectFunctionHandle in the CIN.TDSP LoadDLLLibErr:  An error occurred when loading a function in dsp.dll in the CIN.MDSP NotFindFunctionInDLL:  An error occurred when loading dsp.dll in the CIN.
1029401 DSP GROUP_ERR.  The function ID specified does not belong to any group that is part of the DSP Library currently running on the board.
1029536 DSP FNC_ERR:  The function ID specified does not correspond to a function that is part of the DSP Library currently running on the board.
1029674 DSP NoBrdRespToTransfer:  The DSP board on which you are trying to load the COFF file is not responding to the transfer of the file.  Check if there is a board in the slot desired and verify with the DAQCONF utility.
1029891 DSP AddrSpaceErr:  The COFF file you are trying to load is linked with a memory map that exceeds the maximum memory space allowed by the WE DSP32C chip (2^24).GDSP CoffSectErr:  Found an unimplemented section flag in the COFF file.
1030123 DSP CoffHdrErr:  The file you are attempting to load to the DSP board is not created using the WE DSP32C tools (not an acceptable COFF file).gDSP COFF_FilePathErr:  Could not find the DSP Library file in the directory set by the DAQCONF utility.dDSP TimeOutErr:  The Kernel did not respond or finish function execution in the selected time limit.GDSP HandleAllocErr:  Failed to allocate a handle in the interface code.pDSP HandleSlotErr:  The DSP Handle used does not belong to the same board on which the function request is made.vDSP NotDSPHandle:  The DSP Handle specified is not valid for this board:  it has either been freed or never allocated.tDSP TransferSizeErr:  The size of requested block transfer does not have enough space allocated for it on the board.bDSP ParamSizeErr:  One of the parameters does not have enough space allocated for it on the board.PDSP PtrNotFound:  The DSP address pointer could not be found to free the buffer.

1070376  INSTRUCTIONS:
1070392 Normal Use:  When using subVIs that incorporate the error in/error out (or error I/O) structure, place this handler where you want to inform the user of an error, typically at the end of the I/O data path, as the last action of the program.  If the error in status is ERROR, the handler creates a message describing the error and its source.  If the type of dialog = 1 (default), the message is displayed to the user, who can only acknowedge it.  If the type = 2, the user can acknowledge the message or abort execution; aborting a program with active I/O is not recommended.  If the type = 0, no message is displayed; this is used to process the error programmatically, and the error out cluster elements are wired to individual terminals for that reason.  
1071152 Other Uses:
1071166 local testing.  To test the error code of a subVI or function that does not have the error I/O structure, you can wire its error code and a source string to the local error code and error source inputs.  If error in status indicates no error and error code is not equal to 0, the local code and source are substituted for the error in values, and the status is set TRUE (ERROR).
1071546 user-defined codes.  The error handler has tables of error codes and descriptions for all LabVIEW I/O operations (file, GPIB, DAQ, etc.).  You can augment the tables with the user-defined arrays.  Codes from 5000 to 9999 are reserved for user assignments.
1071803 exception handling.  This mechanism is available either to set the error out status FALSE on what is normally an error or to set the status TRUE on what is normally not an error.  If exception action > 0, the error in code and source are checked.  If they match the exception code and source, the error out status is adjusted accordingly.  That is, if the action = 1, the error out status is set to FALSE and code is set to zero and if the action = 2, the error out is set to TRUE and the code is unchanged.  An empty exception source matches any error in source.  
1072377 . Interpret it bit-wise as follows: x4000: serial port VI error; x0001: receiving queue overflowed or character was received after end-of-file character; x0002: character was lost by overwrite; x0004: parity error; x0008: framing error; x0010: break condition; x0020: CTS timeout; x0040:  DSR timeout; x0080: RLSD timeout; x0100: transmission queue was full when new character arrived; x0200: parallel device timeout; x0400: parallel device I/O error; x0800: parallel device not selected; x1000: parallel device out of paper; x8000: requested mode is  not supported or the idComDev parameter is invalid.  Consult the LabVIEW serial port manual for more information.

1074466 message
1074481 GetCommErr"
1074513 1This error handler is used primarily to inform the user if an input error exists, to describe the error, and to identify where it occurred.  The information for this is derived from the inputs error in, error code, and error source, and from an internal error description table.  The table describes all errors that can be created by LabVIEW or its associated I/O operations.  The handler has provisions to take alternative actions, such as to cancel or set an error status, and to test for and describe user-defined errors.  See instruction on the front panel.
1075078 =type of dialog determines what type dialog box will be displayed, if any. Regardless of its value, the VI outputs error information and message describing the error.
1075249 displays no dialog box. This is useful if you want to have programmatic control over how the error is handled.
1075364 (the default value) displays a dialog box with a single OK button. After the user responds, the VI returns control to the main VI.
1075499 displays a dialog box with buttons allowing the user to either continue or stop. If the user cancels, the VI calls the Stop function to halt execution. 
1075652 HDcode out is the error code indicated by the error in or error code.
1075722 b^exception code is the error code that you want to treat as an exception. By default, it is 0.
1075820 error code is a numeric error code. If error in indicates an error, the VI ignores error code. If not, the VI tests it. A non-zero value signifies an error.
1075979 user-defined codes is an array of the numeric error codes you define in your VIs. The VI searches this array after searching the internal list of error codes. Codes in the range of 5000 to 9999 are reserved for users.
1076199 user-defined descriptions is an array of descriptions of user-defined codes. If an incoming error matches one in user-defined codes, the VI uses the corresponding description from user-defined descriptions in message.
1076417 2.source out indicates the source of the error.
1076465 }yexception source is the error message that you want to use to test for an exception. By default, it is an empty string. 
1076590 error source is an optional string you can use to describe the source of error code. The VI uses the string in message if there is an error.
1076735 exception action is a way for you to create exceptions to error handling. You can treat what is normally an error as no error, or treat a no error condition as an error using this parameter. 
1076931 (the default value) performs no error exception handling. 
1076994 cancels error under the following conditions:
1077042 If the VI detects an error, as described in the status and error code parameters, and if that error code value matches exception code and the error source value matches exception source, the VI sets status out to FALSE, code out to 0, and source out to an empty string. An empty exception source string matches any error source string.
1077382 sets error under the following conditions:
1077427 If the VI detects no error, as described in the status and error code parameters, but the code value of error in matches exception code and the error source value matches exception source, the VI sets status out to TRUE, code out to the code value from error in, and source out to the source value from error in.
1077740 jferror in describes an error that you want to check. If unwired, this VI checks error code for errors.
1077846 status is TRUE if an error occurred. If this value is FALSE, then the error handler assumes that no error occurred according to the error in, and then checks the error code.
1078020 51code is the error code associated with an error.
1078073 source. In case of an error, most VIs that use the error in and error out clusters set source to the name of the VI or function that produced the error.
1078226 |xerror out contains the same information as status out, code out, and source out. It has the same structure as error in.
1078350 status is TRUE if an error occurred. If this value is FALSE, then the error handler assumes that no error occurred according to the error in, and then checks the error code.
1078524 51code is the error code associated with an error.
1078577 source. In case of an error, most VIs that use the error in and error out clusters set source to the name of the VI or function that produced the error.
1078730 mimessage describes the error code that occurred, the source of the error, and a description of the error.

1131802 device
1131816 port number@
1131831 pattern
1131842 port width (8)
1131860 iteration (0:initialize)
1131900 Most applications need only connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.  Connections to other controls and indicators are useful only if specifically needed.
1132079 The Write to Digital Port VI outputs a pattern (in binary) to a specified digital port.  
1132170 You can control the number of lines in a port by the parameter port width.  You also have the option of not reconfiguring the port as an output port with each iteration of the VI by setting the iteration control to a non-zero value.
1132404 Port Width for the Lab boards, SCXI-1200, DAQBox-1200, DIO-24, DIO-32F, DIO-96, and AT-MIO-16D ports 2, 3 and 4 should be at least 8. 
1132540 Please read the DAQ VI Reference Manual for descriptions of Digital Port Configure and Digital Port Write for more information.yudevice is the device number you assigned to the plug-in DAQ board during configuration. This parameter defaults to 1.
1132789 &port width is the total width in bits of the port. For example, you can combine two 4bit ports into an 8-bit port on an MIO board by setting port width to 8. 
1132949 When port width is greater than the physical width of a digital port, the following restrictions apply. The port width must be an integral multiple of the physical port width, and the port numbers in the combined port must begin with the port named by port number and must increase consecutively. For example, if port number is 3 and port width is 24 (bits), the VI uses ports 3, 4, and 5. 
1133342 (U32) pattern: contains the binary data to write to the port. Bit zero is the least significant bit for the port specified by the port number control. 
1133496 M(i32) iteration: controls when the VI performs initialization.  If iteration is 0, the VI configures the port for output and then writes the data.  If iteration is greater than zero, the VI assumes that configuration has already been done and simply writes the data.  You usually wire this input from a While loop iteration terminal.
1133833 )port number specifies the port this VI configures. A port number value of 0 signifies port 0, a port number of 1 signifies port 1, and so on. If you use a digital SCXI module, use the SCx!MDy!0 syntax, where x is the chassis ID and y is the module device number, to specify the port on a module.

1159431 port width (8)@
1159449 pattern
1159460 iteration (0:initialize)
1159500 Most applications need only connect wires to the controls and indicators displayed in bold.  Connections to other controls and indicators are useful only if specifically needed.
1159679 The Read from Digital Port VI reads a user configured digital port.  The reading is displayed as a binary number in [pattern].
1159807 You have the option to not reconfigure the port as an input port by setting the iteration control to a non-zero value. You can also concatenate multiple ports to operate as one large port by using the port width paramter.
1160030 Port Width for the Lab boards, SCXI-1200, DAQBox-1200, DIO-24, DIO-32F, DIO-96, and AT-MIO-16D ports 2, 3 and 4 should be at least 8.
1160165 Please read the DAQ VI Reference Manual for descriptions of Digital Port Configure and Digital Port Read for more information.yudevice is the device number you assigned to the plug-in DAQ board during configuration. This parameter defaults to 1.
1160413 =port width is the total width in bits or the number of lines of the port. For example, you can combine two 4bit ports into an 8-bit port on an MIO board by setting port width to 8. 
1160596 When port width is greater than the physical width of a digital port, the following restrictions apply. The port width must be an integral multiple of the physical port width, and the port numbers in the combined port must begin with the port named by port number and must increase consecutively. For example, if port number is 3 and port width is 24 (bits), the VI uses ports 3, 4, and 5. 
1160989 (U32) pattern: contains the binary data read from the port. Bit zero is the least significant bit from the port specified by the port number control. 
1161142 J(i32) iteration: controls when the VI performs initialization.  If iteration is 0, the VI configures the port for input and then reads the data.  If iteration is greater than zero, the VI assumes that configuration has already been done and simply reads the data.  You usually wire this input from a While loop iteration terminal.
1161476 )port number specifies the port this VI configures. A port number value of 0 signifies port 0, a port number of 1 signifies port 1, and so on. If you use a digital SCXI module, use the SCx!MDy!0 syntax, where x is the chassis ID and y is the module device number, to specify the port on a module.
